=20
Dear Hans=20
=20
RE: Your questions on FF DEF:
=20
1. When unsorted you just leave the field blank. It is optional.
2.1 "commercial size category": This field follows the scale given in
the prior field "Commercial Size category scale ". In the appendix you
can see that there are two valid codes: "EU" and "English". You should
use "EU" which goes from 1 to 7. The note on the field gives the
reference for the definition: "EU-doc 2406/96 and later amendments when
scale is "EU"." This latter note might not be in the version 12 Nov.
Attached is the 11 Dec. version where this is clarified.
2.2 "subsampling category": In the appendix you can see that there are
two valid codes: "Small", "Medium", "Large".
3. How can you then calculate variance? If you do not have it then I
guess that you should give a best possible estimate, but that is more up
to the statisticians to answer this.
=20
Sorry for bringing in a later version than the 12 Nov. There is no
substantial differences, only correction of typos and some added text
for clarification.
=20
I hope this clarifies it.
Best regards
Teunis
=20

<DIV></DIV>Dear colleagues,<BR><BR>There are some weeks now that you =
returned to=20
your lab and were left by yourself for developing COST functions with a=20
nominative task list. It is time before the end of the year to make the =
point=20
and assess where we are.<BR><BR>First of all, I must say I am surprised =
the=20
developer mailing list stayed mute during the weeks following the =
meeting. I'm=20
not sure if everybody is developing by their own, stuck somewhere in =
waiting for=20
other's work, ...<BR>In any case, this is not the right way of doing. If =
you=20
have questions, doubts, suggestions please make use of the mailing=20
list.<BR><BR>For example, we need to ensure consistency between all =
plots during=20
a work session on COST. In order to do so, you must not define specific=20
arguments in your functions, but rather elaborate a generic way of =
defining=20
these so that every funcions refer to them. The ideas so far are (i) to =
develop=20
these arguments in the options() object (COSTcol, COSTpch, ...) or (ii) =
define a=20
control file for all options used for plotting.<BR><BR>There must be =
tens of=20
issues like the one above, but we are not discussing them. It is partly =
my fault=20
of course as I failed to respond to the only question raised so far but =
it is=20
also a community work and we must rely on the expertise from all the=20
others.<BR><BR>May I ask each of you to make the point on his/her own=20
development, summarise the blocking/struggling issues and propose the =
planned=20
programme to achieve the allocated task(s).<BR><BR>Thank you for your=20
attention<BR><BR>Best regards<BR><BR>Joel<BR><BR><SPAN=20
